  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f04b678d-5111-4712-bcfa-c9cf093835b8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer3504437968461730048">An upper-class woman recovering from a suicide attempt, Margaret Prior has begun visiting the women’s ward of Millbank prison, Victorian London’s grimmest jail, as part of her rehabilitative charity work. Amongst Millbank’s murderers and common thieves, Margaret finds herself increasingly fascinated by one apparently innocent inmate, the enigmatic spiritualist Selina Dawes</span>
  <span id="freeText3504437968461730048" style="display:none">An upper-class woman recovering from a suicide attempt, Margaret Prior has begun visiting the women’s ward of Millbank prison, Victorian London’s grimmest jail, as part of her rehabilitative charity work. Amongst Millbank’s murderers and common thieves, Margaret finds herself increasingly fascinated by one apparently innocent inmate, the enigmatic spiritualist Selina Dawes. Selina was imprisoned after a séance she was conducting went horribly awry, leaving an elderly matron dead and a young woman deeply disturbed. Although initially skeptical of Selina’s gifts, Margaret is soon drawn into a twilight world of ghosts and shadows, unruly spirits and unseemly passions, until she is at last driven to concoct a desperate plot to secure Selina’s freedom, and her own.</span>

Another thing is that the time periods did not run chronologically, confusing us more. What eventually happened to Ms Dors and what was this introduction of a baby? Did Margaret eventually kill herself and who was in the coffin? Who was Peter if there was no ghost? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I think it was hinted at that she killed herself.<br />I don't remember a baby or a coffin.<br />Peter wasn't real and he wasn't a ghost. During seances Vigers or<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I think it was hinted at that she killed herself.<br />I don't remember a baby or a coffin.<br />Peter wasn't real and he wasn't a ghost. During seances Vigers or some other assistant would go around touching the women, giving them fruit and so on, as Peter. Since the other women were in the dark and ready to believe, they thought he was real.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1289935-did-anyone-notice-how-the-last-line">Did anyone notice how the last line Margaret wrote in her diary was of her hinting at her suicide, drowning herself in the Thames? Because above all of this, the betrayal and her mental illness, she should have tried to stay strong and patch her life. Maybe buy her new clothes, do anything to disguise how things really happened, then in a few years maybe she met a woman who was for once honest with her. Thoughts?</a>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I didn't see any future for her, given her mother's attitudes about how she should live. And now that she's been swindled out of money, her family wil<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I didn't see any future for her, given her mother's attitudes about how she should live. And now that she's been swindled out of money, her family will restrict her even further. Even if she met a woman who loved her, it seems unlikely that she'll be able to get away. Suicide seemed like the best outcome for her, sadly.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <a title="S.S." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9638684-s-s"><img alt="S.S." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349286052p2/9638684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/426944360?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S.S." class="user" itemprop="url" name="S.S." href="/user/show/9638684-s-s">S.S.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9638684-s-s?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9638684-s-s?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9638684-s-s?shelf=psychological">psychological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9638684-s-s?shelf=sad-ending-oh-god">sad-ending-oh-god</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9638684-s-s?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9638684-s-s?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9638684-s-s?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer426944360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15724673978933032390">Oh, Sarah Waters, the lesbian Charles Dickens. Some think she’s boring and I totally understand that. Nothing can be more mundane than flowing, ornate sentences filled with imagery strong enough to physically transport you to the setting, right? And don’t get me started on that gorgeous historically accurate Victorian-style prose. I’m half asleep just thinking about her engaging plots and characters. So, yeah, I can definitely see how it can be boring and how you’d rather watch football or somet</span>
  <span id="freeText15724673978933032390" style="display:none">Oh, Sarah Waters, the lesbian Charles Dickens. Some think she’s boring and I totally understand that. Nothing can be more mundane than flowing, ornate sentences filled with imagery strong enough to physically transport you to the setting, right? And don’t get me started on that gorgeous historically accurate Victorian-style prose. I’m half asleep just thinking about her engaging plots and characters. So, yeah, I can definitely see how it can be boring and how you’d rather watch football or something.<br /><br />That was sarcasm, by the way.<br /><br />Okay, cutting the crap and getting down to the review. Yes, there will be spoilers.<br /><br /><i>Affinity</i> is about a spinster (an older, unmarried woman) named Margaret Prior and, boy, has life really messed her up. Her father (whom she loved dearly) is dead, her mom is overbearing and protective and a Bible away from being the mom in Carrie, her former (female) lover is married to her brother and they have a child together. She takes chloral every day for her emotional instability/insomnia, eventually using it to aid in her suicide after the death of her father. Her suicide failed, obviously, so she decided to be a Lady Visitor at Millbank prison, spending her days speaking with convicts.<br /><br />At the prison, she meets quirkily alluring and enigmatic Selina Dawes, a psychic medium incarcerated for a reading gone awry. The two seem to be oddly attracted to one another, the nature of their meetings becoming increasingly intimate (on the emotional level, you pervs. Okay, okay, it was supposed to be romantic, but, ya know, jail cells aren’t the most private places).<br /><br />Throughout the whole thing, there’s an overhanging sense of dread and the entire atmosphere of the book is summed up by: <i>something isn’t right here</i>. After all, Selina seems to be the real deal when it comes to mediums and definitely isn’t a fraud. No, ma’am. No way. Nuh uh. Never ever. Totally honest. Yup.<br /><br />Long story short, the ending is a bit of a mindfuck if you’re like me and start thinking <i>after</i> you finish a book, as opposed to during.<br /><br />A handful of other reviews claim that they didn’t care for the character of Margaret Prior, or that they were angry because she was impressionable, weak, and lacked a backbone. I can assume that these people have also never suffered through the trials of uncontrollable bouts of depression, anxiety, self-identity crises, or any other emotional disorders. They probably have thriving social lives and aren’t afraid of things like spiders or airplanes. This isn’t a bad thing, so be glad that your mental health is squeaky clean and you can’t relate to a hopeless and miserable character. I, on the other hand, am utterly neurotic, so Margaret and I got along like two people at an A.A. meeting. To understand her actions, you had to have been familiar with her state of mind. Her obsessiveness and anxiety so mirrored my own, and that was probably the most frightening part of the book.<br /><br />You see, Margaret’s weakness is what drove the plot. Her infatuation and vulnerability is what kept her coming back to Selina time and time again. The way she desperately latched onto her and put her on a pedestal as basically her saving grace was beautiful in itself.<br /><br />Speaking of their relationship, let me talk about that for a bit. It was adorable, in my opinion. At first, you’re really convinced that this is a genuine type of love and that two people truly found each other at a miserable time in their lives and are now destined to defeat the odds and get married and gain weight and watch reality shows together, happily ever after. But this isn’t Nicholas Sparks — this is a Victorian lesbian dark paranormal anguish-filled melodrama, and it wants you to be sad.<br /><br />All in all, this book was fantastic. The plot twist was intricately crafted, almost to an absurd degree. It contained almost everything I’m interested in, which consists of the paranormal, social stigmas, mental instability, Victorian England, betrayal, superb prose, and lesbians.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15724673978933032390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_83617791" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83617791" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83617791?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of gothic literature, Edgar Allen Poe</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=1800s">1800s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=uk">uk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=favorites-all-time">favorites-all-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=lgbtqi">lgbtqi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-ghosts">pn-ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=scared-the-crap-out-of-me">scared-the-crap-out-of-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83617791" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2050593517193444099">In reading the gothic psychological novel <i>Affinity</i>, it is nearly impossible to shake off an overwhelming feeling of gloom and pervasive dread. Following a failed suicide attempt, a young "lady visitor" named Margaret Prior develops a relationship with an inmate named Selina Dawes in a Victorian women's prison, and both their lives are forever changed by their acquaintance.<br/><br/>Narrated in alternating chapters by the two very different women, this dark, moody story incites fear, melancholy, and terrib</span>
  <span id="freeText2050593517193444099" style="display:none">In reading the gothic psychological novel <i>Affinity</i>, it is nearly impossible to shake off an overwhelming feeling of gloom and pervasive dread. Following a failed suicide attempt, a young "lady visitor" named Margaret Prior develops a relationship with an inmate named Selina Dawes in a Victorian women's prison, and both their lives are forever changed by their acquaintance.<br /><br />Narrated in alternating chapters by the two very different women, this dark, moody story incites fear, melancholy, and terrible pity. As always, with this author's work comes a thoroughly researched story and a compelling look at women in oppressive circumstances, as well as how their limited choices often lead to desperate attempts to control their own destinies. There's also an erotic undercurrent of forbidden attraction running deep in this novel as Margaret finds herself increasingly drawn to the mysterious Selina Dawes, who has been imprisoned for a spiritualist reading gone horribly wrong. Their subtly blooming attraction is heightened by the misery of the contrast with Selina's living conditions at Millbank Prison (an <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Millbank_Prison" rel="nofollow noopener">actual London prison</a>, by the way), and it's a certainty that in Margaret's desire to save Selina, she is also desperate to save herself.<br /><br /><i>And what will your sister do if her husband should die, and she should take another? Who will she fly to then, when she has crossed the spheres? For she will fly to someone, we will all fly to someone, we will all return to that piece of shining matter from which our souls are torn with another, two halves of the same. It may be that the husband your sister has now has that other soul, that has affinity with her soul--I hope it is. But it maybe the next man she takes, or it may be neither. It may be someone she would never think to look to on the earth, someone kept from her by some false boundary...</i><br /><br />Sarah Waters writes in dense, elegant prose and tells stories that unfold with exquisite deliberation. <i>Affinity</i> is similar to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6065182.The_Little_Stranger" title="The Little Stranger by Sarah Waters" rel="nofollow noopener">The Little Stranger</a>, in that there are such evocative, spine-chilling moments (including a particularly vivid one involving <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[dripping wax and a dimpled baby's arm :-O  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) that I literally had to put the book down and step away from it. She masterfully creates an atmosphere of suffocating melancholy and builds the tension to an almost unbearable point, so that when the characters finally break, there is a blessed emotional release and relief in the confusion and madness that follows. <br /><br />As with all of the authors' novels, it's important not to read too many reviews or interviews lest important surprises are spoiled. I've read enough of her books to know that I needed to pay attention to every word that is uttered, but she still kept me guessing until the devastating end. If you decide to read this, try to save it for a day when it's cold and dreary and drizzling; I did, and my imagination nearly went wild over the awful conditions of the prison, as well as the evocative seances I could picture perfectly in my mind. <i>Affinity</i> isn't the typical jump-out-of-the-closet horror novel, but for the reader who appreciates subtlety and who might feel a fine shiver when things don't feel <i>quite</i> right in the house, it can offer an incredibly suspenseful and terrifying read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2050593517193444099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_221859873" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221859873" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/221859873?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of quality women's fiction </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=mysteries-thrillers-horror">mysteries-thrillers-horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer221859873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14457504511628267082">As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/3/post/2012/02/affinity-by-sarah-waters.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/>It is almost impossible to say anything about the plot of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72929.Affinity' title='Affinity by Sarah Waters' rel='nofollow noopener'>Affinity</a> without spoiling something, so I'll refrain from recapping. A wealthy, depressed old maid starts visiting a women's prison and quickly finds herself taken by an inmate, a young spiritualist - that's all you need to know.<br/><br/>Let's talk about feelings instead. This sense of emptiness and despair I am left with is so overwhelming right now, that it leads me to believe I might have liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72929.Affinity' title='Affinity by Sarah Waters' rel='nofollow noopener'>Affinity</a> even more than</span>
  <span id="freeText14457504511628267082" style="display:none">As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/3/post/2012/02/affinity-by-sarah-waters.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br /><br />It is almost impossible to say anything about the plot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72929.Affinity" title="Affinity by Sarah Waters" rel="nofollow noopener">Affinity</a> without spoiling something, so I'll refrain from recapping. A wealthy, depressed old maid starts visiting a women's prison and quickly finds herself taken by an inmate, a young spiritualist - that's all you need to know.<br /><br />Let's talk about feelings instead. This sense of emptiness and despair I am left with is so overwhelming right now, that it leads me to believe I might have liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72929.Affinity" title="Affinity by Sarah Waters" rel="nofollow noopener">Affinity</a> even more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45162.Fingersmith" title="Fingersmith by Sarah Waters" rel="nofollow noopener">Fingersmith</a>. I would go as far as to say what I feel now is pretty close to what I felt after finishing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/227614.The_Blind_Assassin" title="The Blind Assassin by Margaret Atwood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Blind Assassin</a>.<br /><br />This novel is very strong as a horror-laden/supernatural mystery - the level of suspense and foreboding is very high, but what it conveys even better is the suffocating atmosphere of oppression, repressed sexuality and thinly veiled eroticism and longing for the forbidden. As a woman of the now I have never experienced such a feeling of being completely powerless first hand, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25334.Sarah_Waters" title="Sarah Waters" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Waters</a> made me feel all of this <i>for</i> her Victorian heroines. <br /><br />Not many contemporary writers can portray this very time- and class-specific environment. It's hard to top <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16.Edith_Wharton" title="Edith Wharton" rel="nofollow noopener">Edith Wharton</a>. But Waters accomplishes it marvelously.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14457504511628267082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Katie Lumsden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8190907-katie-lumsden"><img alt="Katie Lumsden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565906600p2/8190907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2631299393?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie Lumsden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie Lumsden" href="/user/show/8190907-katie-lumsden">Katie Lumsden</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4488859940180610067">I absolutely adored this. Sarah Waters is such an incredible writer and fast becoming one of my favourites. The plotting is brilliant, the themes fascinating, the historical world building spot on, and the charactisation impeccable. Would highly recommend!!</span>

<div id="review_1673024" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1673024" />
    <a title="Siria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/115473-siria"><img alt="Siria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332731316p2/115473.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1673024?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siria" href="/user/show/115473-siria">Siria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115473-siria?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115473-siria?shelf=british-fiction">british-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115473-siria?shelf=queer-lit">queer-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115473-siria?shelf=21st-century">21st-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1673024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14917318251710836327">Sarah Waters, at this stage, must be the accepted queen of Victorian Gothic lesbian melodrama; not, I imagine, that there is much competition for this title, but I think it's a deserved one nonetheless.<br/><br/>In many ways, the plot of <i>Affinity</i> is like that of the other work of Waters' that I have read, <i>Fingersmith</i>. Crime and Victorian punishment, repression and sexuality and psychology, all feature heavily in both books. <i>Affinity</i>, however, is a much more satisfying novel for me. While it, too, hangs on</span>
  <span id="freeText14917318251710836327" style="display:none">Sarah Waters, at this stage, must be the accepted queen of Victorian Gothic lesbian melodrama; not, I imagine, that there is much competition for this title, but I think it's a deserved one nonetheless.<br /><br />In many ways, the plot of <i>Affinity</i> is like that of the other work of Waters' that I have read, <i>Fingersmith</i>. Crime and Victorian punishment, repression and sexuality and psychology, all feature heavily in both books. <i>Affinity</i>, however, is a much more satisfying novel for me. While it, too, hangs on some often surprising twists of coincidence, these twists are orchestrated by an intelligence that is much more subtle and convincing, to my mind, than the occurrences in <i>Fingersmith</i> (I found those to be much too Dickensian, and I loathe Dickens). And while, admittedly, I never came to feel terribly attached to and moved by Margaret and her plight - she was a little too detached, and her fate a little too obviously signposted - she was undoubtedly a well-drawn character.<br /><br />The real achievement of the book, though, is the sense of period and atmosphere and mood it has. When I closed the book, I had the strongest desire to open all the windows in the room, because I needed sunlight and wind, after spending so long in the airless world that Waters created. It's rare anymore that a book has that effect on me, so I do think that this is one that I will be re-reading and savouring.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1217767995" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1217767995" />
    <a title="Vonia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5204784-vonia"><img alt="Vonia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584439676p2/5204784.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1217767995?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vonia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vonia" href="/user/show/5204784-vonia">Vonia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=ghosts-spiritual">ghosts-spiritual</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=propriety">propriety</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5204784-vonia?shelf=isolated-setting">isolated-setting</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1217767995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1822768600477239693">I have said it before, I will say it again. I cannot fathom how Sarah Waters does it, how she can draw the reader into this entirely other world, this other period, time, place, complete immersion. Even something simple like the protagonist Miss Prior's afternoon in The Spiritualists' Reading Room instantly conceived for me a dim, smoky, velvet lined library where she learns the secrets of her true love/affinity's case. Genius. <br/><br/>I honestly do not typically care for the paranormal stories, but und</span>
  <span id="freeText1822768600477239693" style="display:none">I have said it before, I will say it again. I cannot fathom how Sarah Waters does it, how she can draw the reader into this entirely other world, this other period, time, place, complete immersion. Even something simple like the protagonist Miss Prior's afternoon in The Spiritualists' Reading Room instantly conceived for me a dim, smoky, velvet lined library where she learns the secrets of her true love/affinity's case. Genius. <br /><br />I honestly do not typically care for the paranormal stories, but under the guidance of Waters, a pretty great read. With the unexpected ending, I admit I did not like it, but then again, I guess it was good, in that way only great writers can have me appreciating an otherwise unacceptable 180. In my opinion, the author better have a damn good reason as well as some damn good transitioning with foreshadowing for these endings. <br /><br />Selina Dawes. What a character. She had me good. I will say that. I guess I was not paying attention, so enraptured by Waters' writing, I was. At least that is what I say. I feel like I should have seen it from a million miles away. Her story was very interesting, although I do wish there was more detail, more insight into her childhood. In fact, I felt like the center of the story told was quite intense, extremely well told, even a little long, but could have used more insight into "Miss Prior"/Aurora's history, both before + after. <br /><br />As for the Spiritualism, ghosts, seances, readings, etcetera, I actually really liked reading these aspects of the novel, appreciating Waters' obvious research into the themes. <br /><br />Oh, Sarah Waters, how I love thee. <br /></span>

<div id="review_132757015" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132757015" />
    <a title="Misha Mathew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3809685-misha-mathew"><img alt="Misha Mathew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388910909p2/3809685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132757015?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misha Mathew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misha Mathew" href="/user/show/3809685-misha-mathew">Misha Mathew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3809685-misha-mathew?shelf=mystery-suspense-thriller">mystery-suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3809685-misha-mathew?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3809685-misha-mathew?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3809685-misha-mathew?shelf=history">history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132757015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer83395536356131330">"Sexy, Spooky, Stylish" - that's the blurb on the cover. If I was not a Sarah Waters fan already, I would have picked up the book based on those words. How can you resist a book with that description? After reading the book, I can safely say that those words are an accurate description of Affinity. I will further add to that - "Haunting and magical."<br/><br/>It seems, I have been reading many deliciously gothic novels recently. Well, I am not complaining! Affinity is yet another addition to my love for a</span>
  <span id="freeText83395536356131330" style="display:none">"Sexy, Spooky, Stylish" - that's the blurb on the cover. If I was not a Sarah Waters fan already, I would have picked up the book based on those words. How can you resist a book with that description? After reading the book, I can safely say that those words are an accurate description of Affinity. I will further add to that - "Haunting and magical."<br /><br />It seems, I have been reading many deliciously gothic novels recently. Well, I am not complaining! Affinity is yet another addition to my love for anything gothic. Sarah Waters, who is considered the "Queen of Victorian Gothic novels", churns out yet another winner.<br /><br />Margaret Prior suffers a complete mental breakdown, following her father's death. A failed suicide attempt breaks her even further. She lives with her domineering mother and a sister, who will soon be married. Margaret feels jealous because she thinks, by marrying, her sister will somehow "evolve" while she will remain stagnant. She's constantly under her mother's watchful eyes and is treated like an imbecile. Her former lover, Helen, is now married to her brother - a fact that she is still unable to get over. Margaret is a repressed, closed-up young woman with no hopes for the future.<br /><br />In order to forget her painful past, she becomes a "lady visitor" at Millbank Prison. Her job is to talk to the women prisoners, listen to them and guide them towards a more positive direction. She's drawn towards one particular prisoner, Selina Dawes, a spiritualist and a psychic medium, who has been imprisoned for assaulting one of her clients.<br /><br />When you love an author a lot, you tend to develop gigantic expectations from all of that author's books, which is probably unfair. I have not been very subtle about my love for Sarah Waters. Fingersmith and The Little Stranger are not only my favorite books by her, but are also my all-time favorites as well. Perhaps my expectations were very unrealistic. In the beginning I felt a little deflated. Don't get me wrong. The beginning was compelling enough to keep me reading on, but it was just not up to the admittedly unrealistic standards I have set for Sarah Waters' novels. However, this feeling did not last long as the book soon picked up and I was hooked!<br /><br />Affinity is told from both Selina's and Margaret's perspectives. The reader feels as fascinated by Selina as Margaret is. Yet, she still remains an enigma, a mystery throughout the book. The story unfolds slowly, with each chapter pulling you in completely.<br /><br />Selina is viewed as a charlatan, a fraud and a cheat. But the time spent talking to her each day convinces Margaret of her truth. Moreover, there are some strange, extraordinary events which provide further proof of Selina's powers. With each meeting, the magnetic pull , which Margaret feels towards Selina intensifies, leading towards the ultimately shocking conclusion.<br /><br /><i>"We are the same, you and I. We have seen cut, two halves, from the same piece of shining matter. Oh, I could say, I love you—that is a simple thing to say . . . But my spirit does not love yours—it is entwined with it. Our flesh does not love: our flesh is the same . . ." </i> <br /><br />I deeply felt for Margaret. I felt her frustration and how repressed she was. I can understand how suffocated she felt under her mother's constant nagging. One of the most powerful aspects of Affinity is the setting and the atmosphere the author creates. Millbank prison is like a character in itself - the author's descriptions of the prison is so vivid that you can feel the prisoners' predicament in the controlled and suffocating environment. <br /><br />Margaret's longing for Selina, the unspoken but intense "forbidden" emotions and her unhappiness is heartrending and hits you hard.<br /><i><br /> It is as if every poet who ever wrote a line to his own love wrote secretly for me, and for Selina. My blood - even as I write this- my blood , my muscle and every fibre of me, is listening, for her. When I sleep, it is to dream of her. When shadows move across my eye, it is to dream of her, I know them now for shadows of her. My room is still, but never silent - I hear her heart, beating across the night in time to my own.<br /></i><br /><br />Margaret's stark despair and misery really got to me. My heart was breaking for her all throughout. Sarah Waters has an incredible ability to make you care so much for the characters that they almost become real people to you.<br />Selina's descriptions of her life as a medium and her ability to contact spirits is so real and even mesmerizing, that you believe her without questions or skepticism. Her conversations with the spirits and her experiences creeped me out quite a bit. It unnerved me and fascinated me at the same time.<br /><br />Like most of author's other novels, Affinity has females as the main protagonists and is set in the Victorian era. In addition, the author has eloquently tackled subjects like repression, sexual awakening and spirituality. Three are several feminist elements as well. The author, very subtly, raises questions about a woman's place in the society.<br /><i><br />"Why do gentlemen's voices carry so clearly, when women's are so easily stifled?" </i><br /><br /><br />Margaret, though technically a "free" woman, is still a prisoner - to her gender, to her circumstances and to her mother's wishes.<br /><i><br /> " Women are bred to do more of the same - that is their function. It is only ladies like me that throw the system out, make it stagger..."<br /><br /></i><br />The ending is probably the best part of the book. I am still reeling from the shock of the end. It was so unexpected; I doubt anyone could have seen it coming. To say I am impressed is an understatement.<br /><br />Like every other Sarah Waters' books, Affinity will remain with me for a long time to come. If I had not read any other books by this author, it would have been a 5 star read for me. Affinity, in my opinion, is not her best, but still a fantastic read. Sarah Wates' lyrical writing makes every book worth it.<br /><br />Now I just have two more books by Sarah Waters to read and then begins the long painful wait for her next book. I believe I can gobble up all of Sarah Waters' books in one go and yet be hungry for more of her brilliance.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="83395536356131330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_46435592" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46435592" />
    <a title="Anastasia Garcia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2034910-anastasia-garcia"><img alt="Anastasia Garcia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489804701p2/2034910.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46435592?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anastasia Garcia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anastasia Garcia" href="/user/show/2034910-anastasia-garcia">Anastasia Garcia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781573221566" href="/book/show/849180.Affinity">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46435592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11229759992307696784">Generally, I don't pick up random books at Barnes and Noble that I don't already know a little about. However, I made an exception with Affinity because it intrigued me so. I come to find out that was a pretty costly mistake. <br/><br/>Firstly, the book dabbles in the supernatural psychics world which I already hold a serious distrust for. However, I thought this book might present the spiritual medium's world in a light that's a little more pretty and entertaining. No, instead I still feel oddly at ends </span>
  <span id="freeText11229759992307696784" style="display:none">Generally, I don't pick up random books at Barnes and Noble that I don't already know a little about. However, I made an exception with Affinity because it intrigued me so. I come to find out that was a pretty costly mistake. <br /><br />Firstly, the book dabbles in the supernatural psychics world which I already hold a serious distrust for. However, I thought this book might present the spiritual medium's world in a light that's a little more pretty and entertaining. No, instead I still feel oddly at ends with the character Selina, who is a medium in jail for a crime relating to her seances. This distrust grows and grows until the climax of the book where it tops off as disdain, ending with me disgusted with the main character a delicate woman by the name of Margaret.<br /><br />Secondly, I disapprove of the frailty of women back before the turn of the century. This book is entirely devoted to a main character who can't deal with situations with a level head or a rational outlook. Instead she is swayed by every emotion possible, sometimes resorting to drugs to deal with her "horrible headaches." She faints at every instance, "feels ill" any time there's confrontation and tends to side with her romantic view of people which ends up costing her dearly. I disapprove of her melancholy methods of dealing with her grief and I also disapprove of her inability to assert herself or read people truthfully. <br /><br />Thirdly, the book is developed slowly and very wordy. Pages are drawn out in a way that's neither enticing or beautiful, but more lengthy and boring. I felt as if I was pushing over words to get the point towards the end of the book. The character's a built for chapters and chapters, and I disapproved of the somewhat lesbian relationship that developed, not because it consisted of two females but because it was stupid and based on nothing substantial. Margaret needed SOMETHING to cling to and it ends up being an incredibly stupid thing for her to do. More proof that delicate, unsteady women prove to be dumb in the end. <br /><br />On a nicer note, I awarded this book two stars because it DID catch my attention towards the end after the climax. Although I already knew the ending because I could read through the character's emotions straight to the facts and the proper villains. I was frantically turning pages at the end hoping to get to the final conclusion, proof that my speculations were correct. As they were. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11229759992307696784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1775922254" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1775922254" />
    <a title="Primrose Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28497722-primrose-jess"><img alt="Primrose Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605701012p2/28497722.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1775922254?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Primrose Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Primrose Jess" href="/user/show/28497722-primrose-jess">Primrose Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/25337939-affinity">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1775922254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6323247797475735716"> Have you ever read a book and experienced de ja vu at the ending??? I thought this book was one I haven't read before (I still think so) but at the end.. it seemed vaguely familiar as if I had read it. I wasn't too surprised and thought "Wait.. I think I read this before." Chalk it up to the creepy experiences that Margaret Prior experiences through out the book. <br/><br/>My thoughts/reactions:<br/><br/>-The Victorian prison system was abysmal for inmates. The idea of spending years with the notion of no news of </span>
  <span id="freeText6323247797475735716" style="display:none"> Have you ever read a book and experienced de ja vu at the ending??? I thought this book was one I haven't read before (I still think so) but at the end.. it seemed vaguely familiar as if I had read it. I wasn't too surprised and thought "Wait.. I think I read this before." Chalk it up to the creepy experiences that Margaret Prior experiences through out the book. <br /><br />My thoughts/reactions:<br /><br />-The Victorian prison system was abysmal for inmates. The idea of spending years with the notion of no news of the outside, four visits from family a year, questionable food quality, poor healthcare in poor living conditions, religious reading only, nothing to write with, and your entire focus should be rethinking your life choices and how to be better. It made me wonder if this actually worked as a crime deterrent. There is a repeat inmate in the book so I'm not sure how well it works. <br />-As a woman, you could be imprisoned for a suicide attempt. One inmate made it to the second level for her 7 suicide attempts. She was deemed "a public nuisance". Appalling. It makes one wonder how many inmates were truly criminal or suffering from mental illness. <br />-Work must have been so bad there for women to purposefully maim themselves in the forms of tying a rusted button to a cut to induce septicemia, gouging an eye out with a butter knife, swallowing glass, attempting to hang oneself, etc. <br />-For a time period known for it's rigidity and devotion to public propriety; the Victorians were a dramatic emotional lot. It it seemed extremely evident in their writings. I won't sugar coat it; the main character was beginning to get on my nerves with her ruminations and dramatic thinking. Skip the chloral and laudanum... give the girl an SSRI stat. <br />-I think keeping people's hair is so creepy. Sleeping with a braid of hair even more so. <br />-It was an interesting read that at times did creep me out but I didn't respond to this book's alleged "chilling" story as many reviewers or book bloggers seemed to. Except for the wax scene in the prison cell; that gave me the creeps. <br /> - This is definitely a thinking sort of a read. I'm sure the more I mull it over; more thoughts on it will come to me. It is incredibly well written. I'd love to hear Waters lecture on the time period. She knows her stuff and crafts a good tale. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6323247797475735716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1080748281" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1080748281" />
    <a title="BrokenTune" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10592271-brokentune"><img alt="BrokenTune" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391017756p2/10592271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1080748281?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BrokenTune" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BrokenTune" href="/user/show/10592271-brokentune">BrokenTune</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/18719763-affinity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10592271-brokentune?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1080748281" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15492403669811242292"><i>"Now I have more freedom than I ever had at any time in my life, and I do only the things I always have."</i><br/> <br/>Affinity - a feeling of closeness and understanding that someone has for another person because of their similar qualities, ideas, or interests.<br/> <br/>This book was not easy to get into. I'm neither a fan of Dickensian tales of woe nor of paranormal or supernatural stories, so for most of this book I was not convinced I would finish it, never mind like it. <br/> <br/>The structure of the book was difficult,</span>
  <span id="freeText15492403669811242292" style="display:none"><i>"Now I have more freedom than I ever had at any time in my life, and I do only the things I always have."</i><br /> <br />Affinity - a feeling of closeness and understanding that someone has for another person because of their similar qualities, ideas, or interests.<br /> <br />This book was not easy to get into. I'm neither a fan of Dickensian tales of woe nor of paranormal or supernatural stories, so for most of this book I was not convinced I would finish it, never mind like it. <br /> <br />The structure of the book was difficult, too. Chapters jump back and forth in time, and the narrative changes between the characters. I kept having to go back and re-read passages to remember where about in the story I was at - and which character.<br /> <br />However, Waters' writing detailing delicious descriptions of life in a Victorian women's prison was awesome. So awesome in fact that I felt like I was there in the bleak and rigid clasp of fear and despair - haunted (haha) by the question if the supernatural could be real. In fact, having read most of the book at night now that the darkness has gripped us up here in the North, made Affinity the perfect read in the run up to Halloween.<br /> <br />Affinity, as the title suggests, explores the relationship between different people, focusing mostly on upper-middle-class Margaret Prior, who volunteers to become a lady visitor in a London prison, and Selina Dawes, a notorius medium who has been sent down after being involved in a woman's death. However, affinity applies to other relationships in the book and each of them serves to paint a picture of the main character, Margaret Prior, and her struggle with life in London society during the 1870s. <br /> <br />As I mentioned, the book was a bit of a struggle for me at first but very rewarding in the end. The ending it self has been criticised by others, but I thought it was perfectly fitting, though not anywhere near as polished as the ending Waters' later books.<br /><br /><br />This review was originally posted on BookLikes: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://brokentune.booklikes.com/post/1028682/affinity">http://brokentune.booklikes.com/post/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15492403669811242292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1860557003" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1860557003" />
    <a title="Elizabeth (Alaska)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2026178-elizabeth-alaska"><img alt="Elizabeth (Alaska)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304966095p2/2026178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1860557003?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth (Alaska)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth (Alaska)" href="/user/show/2026178-elizabeth-alaska">Elizabeth (Alaska)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6641363-affinity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=20th-c-women-read">20th-c-women-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=xx-2017-women">xx-2017-women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=late-20th-century">late-20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=women">women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=xx-2017-reps">xx-2017-reps</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1860557003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14957276984468002209">Sarah Waters sets the atmosphere of this early on. Does gothic always take place at an old mansion hidden in fog? No, here it is Millbank prison on the banks of the Thames River. Let's not forget the spirits that we can expect in a gothic novel - certainly Sarah Waters has not.<blockquote>To Millbank. It is only a week since my last visit, but the mood of the prison has shifted, as if with the season, and it is a darker and more bitter place now, than ever. The towers seemed to have grown higher and broader</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14957276984468002209" style="display:none">Sarah Waters sets the atmosphere of this early on. Does gothic always take place at an old mansion hidden in fog? No, here it is Millbank prison on the banks of the Thames River. Let's not forget the spirits that we can expect in a gothic novel - certainly Sarah Waters has not.<blockquote>To Millbank. It is only a week since my last visit, but the mood of the prison has shifted, as if with the season, and it is a darker and more bitter place now, than ever. The towers seemed to have grown higher and broader, and the windows to have shrunk; the very scents of the place seemed to have changed, since I last went there—the grounds smelling of fog and of chimney smoke as well as of sedge, and the wards reeking of nuisance-buckets still, of cramped and unwashed hair and flesh and mouths, but also of gas, and rust, and sickness. There are great black, blistering radiators at the angle of the passages, and these make the corridors very airless and close.</blockquote>This is written in series of journal entries by the two main characters. They do not alternate, but are interspersed. The chapters are dates, and from this is easily understood from whose journal we are reading. In this way, not only is the story told - a story, which as it progressed was more and more compelling - but also the characters are developed. I said elsewhere that sometimes first person narratives are not always reliable. Let me just admit that I am gullible. <br /><br />I really like books where there are a couple of sentences that give context for the title. <blockquote>Who will she fly to then, when she has crossed the spheres? For she will fly to someone, we will all fly to someone, we will all return to that piece of shining matter from which our souls were torn with another, two halves of the same. It may be that the husband your sister has now has that other soul, that has the affinity with her soul—I hope it is. But it may be the next man she takes, or it may be neither.</blockquote>And<blockquote> I looked only at her, heard her voice only; and when I spoke at last, it was to ask her this: ‘How will a person know, Selina, when the soul that has the affinity with hers is near it?’</blockquote>I have read just one other by Sarah Waters - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8913370.Fingersmith" title="Fingersmith by Sarah Waters" rel="nofollow noopener">Fingersmith</a>. Her prose is interesting: neither does it rely on simple sentence structure and vocabulary, nor is it so convoluted that the reader is lost along the way. You can depend on an LGBT focus in the main characters, but without being hit over the head with it. The characters are what they are, the story line and characterizations make no attempt to convince the reader that life is unfair because of sexual orientation. Life may be unfair, but isn't it so in some way for everyone? <br /><br />This title is less well known than her others, but I think it should be otherwise. Another 5-star read for me. I'm on a roll.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14957276984468002209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2769381891" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1396335-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442451149p2/1396335.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2769381891" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5406468122728089926">Another extraordinary novel from Sarah Waters. I can't believe I'm only just now discovering these books. I'm amazed by her range and her ability to conjure another era in such an all-absorbing, spellbinding way. This one is an absolutely perfect Gothic mystery/tragedy/ghost story, set in a Victorian-era women's prison. If you read Daphne du Maurier's Rebecca and felt like you'd never read anything as good again--well, it's time to get to know Sarah Waters.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_123673002" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123673002" />
    <a title="Celine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3387843-celine"><img alt="Celine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460292659p2/3387843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123673002?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celine" href="/user/show/3387843-celine">Celine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=lgbt-queer">lgbt-queer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123673002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11605075621468685557">When I started this book, I had no idea how sad <i>Affinity</i> would make me. Because it does, and it has, for at least two days even after finishing the book.<br/><br/><i>Affinity</i> is the tale Margaret, a young lady living in nineteenth-century London. After her father's death, Margaret has fallen ill for half a year. Now everything is slightly better, she has taken it upon her to visit the female inmates at the Millbank prison as Lady Visitor. Here she meets the spirit medium Serena, who starts to intrigue her mo</span>
  <span id="freeText11605075621468685557" style="display:none">When I started this book, I had no idea how sad <i>Affinity</i> would make me. Because it does, and it has, for at least two days even after finishing the book.<br /><br /><i>Affinity</i> is the tale Margaret, a young lady living in nineteenth-century London. After her father's death, Margaret has fallen ill for half a year. Now everything is slightly better, she has taken it upon her to visit the female inmates at the Millbank prison as Lady Visitor. Here she meets the spirit medium Serena, who starts to intrigue her more with every visit.<br /><br />This novel unfolds very, very, very slowly. It's way shorter than the other book I have read by Sarah Waters, <i>Fingersmith</i>, but it doesn't contain as many plot twists as that one does. <i>Affinity</i> feels a lot slower. I didn't mind that much, because I happen to love the historical period, and I can easily be entertained by the gloomy mood. Still, after a while I started to wish for the end, because about ninety percent of this novel is build-up. <br /><br />And when the end comes, it hits hard. I won't spoil anything for you, but I can assure you that if you have come to be affectionate towards any of the characters, it will stay with you. I personally didn't see it coming it all. It all wraps up neatly together, but not in a way you would normally get with this type of novel.<br /><br />The character of Margaret is a very flawed one. We see most of the story through her eyes, and her weakness shows through every experience she has. She's not very easy to like, but I really did want her to get a happy ending, in any form or another. Madness, substance abuse and depression are a few of the underlying themes, but I wish they were more pronounced. Without explaining Margaret's mental condition, she's really just a weak woman that doesn't appreciate the things she has in life. <br /><br /><i>Affinity</i>'s strength is the vividness of the descriptions of Millbank. I could perfectly imagine the creaking iron, the cold labyrinth-like corridors, the sound of a key turning in its lock. Ms Waters is a master in painting a gloomy atmosphere. <br /><br />I recommend this book if you really feel like reading something that will make you shiver. It's not as accessible as <i>Fingersmith</i> is, but it's still a great historical novel. Not for the inexperienced reader, as the novel is written in slightly lofty archaic language and style. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11605075621468685557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_739641660" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/739641660" />
    <a title="Rusalka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6163718-rusalka"><img alt="Rusalka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591511894p2/6163718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/739641660?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rusalka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rusalka" href="/user/show/6163718-rusalka">Rusalka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781860496929" href="/book/show/392636.Affinity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=ylto-group-theme-reads">ylto-group-theme-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=europe">europe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=uk">uk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=lgbti">lgbti</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6163718-rusalka?shelf=ylto-chunksters-gap-fillers">ylto-chunksters-gap-fillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer739641660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15839848506688542091">Sticking with the gothic theme for a bit. Affinity is a book I actually hadn't heard that much about. But after loving <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/56373.Tipping_the_Velvet' title='Tipping the Velvet by Sarah Waters' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tipping the Velvet</a> so much last year, the last time I was at the secondhand bookshop I picked it up. Which was fortuitous as there were a few other Sarah Waters options, but this was the one chosen as a group read for April.<br/><br/>The book is another Victorian London historical fiction. We meet Margaret, the eldest, single sister in her family, as she starts her first day as a Lady Vis</span>
  <span id="freeText15839848506688542091" style="display:none">Sticking with the gothic theme for a bit. Affinity is a book I actually hadn't heard that much about. But after loving <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/56373.Tipping_the_Velvet" title="Tipping the Velvet by Sarah Waters" rel="nofollow noopener">Tipping the Velvet</a> so much last year, the last time I was at the secondhand bookshop I picked it up. Which was fortuitous as there were a few other Sarah Waters options, but this was the one chosen as a group read for April.<br /><br />The book is another Victorian London historical fiction. We meet Margaret, the eldest, single sister in her family, as she starts her first day as a Lady Visitor to the infamous <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Millbank_Prison" rel="nofollow noopener">Millbank prison</a>. Millbank is not a particularly nice place. At least by this stage, the worst prisoners in England were sent to another prison in London, but this was still not a nice place to end up at all.<br /><br />Inside Millbank, Margaret meets a prisoner called Selina, who is a spiritualist. We all know how fascinated the Victorians were with the occult, spirits, magic and the like, so it isn't a surprise that Margaret is fascinated with Selina and her abilities, and ends up being drawn in deeper and deeper.<br /><br />Right, so, we can all guess by now that I am a skeptic. In my experience these kind of people prey on people desperate for a message from someone they throw tells and information into the medium's lap. HOWEVER, the disclaimer for this book is that I wanted it to be all true for the story. I am never one to let facts get in the way of a good story. Unless you swear to me something is a scientific fact and it is blatantly wrong. That pisses me off. Otherwise, I'm all for a bit of fun.<br /><br />And while I wouldn't describe this book as fun, and while I couldn't completely disengage my disbelief this book drew me along quicker than I would have thought. And talk about a twisty ending!! I was hanging around 3 stars until I started hitting the twists. I didn't like it as much as Tipping the Velvet. I thought it may have been her first book, but looks like it was the second. And then it struck me, that was the problem with this book. It had a lot of second album syndrome to it. It wasn't bad, just felt a bit rushed and not quite as thought through as that debut.<br /><br />A short review I know, but still a fun and surprising Victorian, gothic read.<br /><br />For more reviews visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://rusalkii.blogspot.com.au/">http://rusalkii.blogspot.com.au/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15839848506688542091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3045957014" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3045957014" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4784586-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373481234p2/4784586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3045957014?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/4784586-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841978819" href="/book/show/6900418-affinity">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Andrea by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4490376-sarah-mac">Sarah Mac</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=novels">novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3045957014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10689338079732278514">It's not very often I devour a book in a little over a day (knowing Sarah Waters' fondness of sucker-punch plot twists at the last moment, I had the good sense to set it aside in the evening and not stay up all night reading…), and even rarer that I whole-heartedly agree with a blurb.<br/><br/><i>By the time it all begins to matter, you'll find yourself desperately wanting to believe in magic.</i><br/><br/>True. So true… I really wished right until the end <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[this wouldn't be another bleak un-happy ending for </span></span>
  <span id="freeText10689338079732278514" style="display:none">It's not very often I devour a book in a little over a day (knowing Sarah Waters' fondness of sucker-punch plot twists at the last moment, I had the good sense to set it aside in the evening and not stay up all night reading…), and even rarer that I whole-heartedly agree with a blurb.<br /><br /><i>By the time it all begins to matter, you'll find yourself desperately wanting to believe in magic.</i><br /><br />True. So true… I really wished right until the end <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[this wouldn't be another bleak un-happy ending for everyone involved. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This is one of the most atmospheric, creepy books I've read since. Well, since the last time I picked up one of Waters' books. I read it on a dreary, rainy, windy, icy-cold day, and I couldn't have asked for a better setting. Seriously, the woman's writing just creeps me out. I'm just in awe of her talent. There comes a time where you wonder who's really in a prison, Selina in her cell at Millbank, or Margaret in her nice house. <br /><br />I don't think it will replace <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8913370.Fingersmith" title="Fingersmith by Sarah Waters" rel="nofollow noopener">Fingersmith</a> as my favorite Waters book to date, but it's definitely a very close second. It kept me fully enthralled from start to finish, even if it was depressing as hell, and the ending is just evil. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10689338079732278514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
